    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<span id="freeTextContainer9817292773903160373">A small Georgia town erupts in panic when a young college professor is found brutally mutilated in the local diner. But it's only when town pediatrician and coroner Sara Linton does the autopsy that the full extent of the killer's twisted work becomes clear. Sara's ex-husband, police chief Jeffrey Tolliver, leads the investigation -- a trail of terror that grows increasing</span>
  <span id="freeText9817292773903160373" style="display:none">A small Georgia town erupts in panic when a young college professor is found brutally mutilated in the local diner. But it's only when town pediatrician and coroner Sara Linton does the autopsy that the full extent of the killer's twisted work becomes clear. Sara's ex-husband, police chief Jeffrey Tolliver, leads the investigation -- a trail of terror that grows increasingly macabre when another local woman is found crucified a few days later. But he's got more than a sadistic serial killer on his hands, for the county's sole female detective, Lena Adams -- the first victim's sister -- wants to serve her own justice. But it is Sara who holds the key to finding the killer. A secret from her past could unmask the brilliantly malevolent psychopath .. or mean her death.</span>

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2832972793" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5786582946317724634">I don’t find myself in this situation often enough, attempting to put my thoughts on display for a book—and series—that I’ve not only <b>adored for years</b>, but read countless times. Let’s be honest rereads have been an infrequent occurrence in my world. My best guess at the number of trips I’ve made to <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/series/43676-grant-county' rel='nofollow noopener'>Grant County</a> over the years though, six? Yeah, I’m going with six, at least. <br/><br/>While I was the furthest thing from blindsided, I remembered about 98.99% of the plot going in, I still relished <i>every</i> sing</span>
  <span id="freeText5786582946317724634" style="display:none">I don’t find myself in this situation often enough, attempting to put my thoughts on display for a book—and series—that I’ve not only <b>adored for years</b>, but read countless times. Let’s be honest rereads have been an infrequent occurrence in my world. My best guess at the number of trips I’ve made to <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/series/43676-grant-county" rel="nofollow noopener">Grant County</a> over the years though, six? Yeah, I’m going with six, at least. <br /><br />While I was the furthest thing from blindsided, I remembered about 98.99% of the plot going in, I still relished <i>every</i> single moment. Maybe even appreciated the setting a tad more, considering I now call the peach state home.<br /><br />There are countless reasons why <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12504.Karin_Slaughter" title="Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Karin Slaughter</a>’s name has resided at the top of my list of favorite authors over the years. Without getting ahead of myself too much here, I respect the direction she takes this series, despite the sopping mess I always seem to revert to in the end. <br /><br />The main reason why I’ve gravitated towards Slaughter’s work, time and again, continues to be her uncanny ability to deliver an exceptional literary journey and to do so on multiple fronts—clever plotting, unrelenting suspense, detailed but interesting criminal cases, and the characters I love and love to hate. And of course, I can’t downplay the guts and gore. With a name like Slaughter, would you expect anything less than blood-soaked pages and a depraved killer? I think not.<br /><br />The brutal murder (<i>get ready for the heinous happenings</i>) of a college professor rocks the small Georgia town of Heartsdale. Landing Jeffrey, Grant County’s chief of police, and his ex-wife Sara, the County’s pediatrician, and part-time coroner, side-by-side as they work to track down the brazen killer. Tensions rise as the body count increases, and the couple's history comes to a head. The intensity of Jeffrey (<i>love him!</i>) and Sara’s (<i>and her!</i>) connection begs the question—will they, or won’t they?<br /><br />All you love story avoiders, don't let what I'm about to delve into scare you off, this is far from a romance novel. When I first stepped foot in Grant County, I was nowhere near the seasoned romance reader I consider myself to be now. And yet, it was the thoughts and feelings Jeffrey and Sara's connection inspired that ultimately turned this first-time Slaughter reader into a total fangirl. To this day, second-chance storylines hold a special place in my heart, with all the credit going to Jeffrey and Sara. Their relationship arc is extremely well-done. Maybe even monumental, as far as second-chances go. I'm talking favorite literary couple territory here.<br /><br /><blockquote>“Sometimes,” he began, “when I wake up in the morning, I forget that you’re not there. I forget that I lost you.”</blockquote><br /><br />The small town setting, interesting characters (<i>some are easy to adore, while others will naturally piss you off</i>) and the depravity put on full display, makes this one heck of a series opener. Even almost 18 years after release (Wow!; first published in September 2001) and several revisits, <b>I <u>still</u> remain impressed</b>.</span>
  <a data-text-id="5786582946317724634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer17898617266437411789"><b>4.5 Stars<br/><br/>Thank you Karin Slaughter for restoring my faith in thrillers! </b><br/><br/>The thrillers I have been reading lately have been sub-par. I was considering taking a break from the genre, but then I read <i>Blindsighted</i> and it reminded me why I love thrillers. This book is what a thriller should be: Dark, multilayered, suspenseful and so much more. It is gruesome and brutal and there is a level of depravity that made me squirm. I loved both Sara and Jeffrey’s characters. Their voices are strong and their </span>
  <span id="freeText17898617266437411789" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Stars<br /><br />Thank you Karin Slaughter for restoring my faith in thrillers! </b><br /><br />The thrillers I have been reading lately have been sub-par. I was considering taking a break from the genre, but then I read <i>Blindsighted</i> and it reminded me why I love thrillers. This book is what a thriller should be: Dark, multilayered, suspenseful and so much more. It is gruesome and brutal and there is a level of depravity that made me squirm. I loved both Sara and Jeffrey’s characters. Their voices are strong and their characters are multi-dimensional. <br /><br />Thank you to my GR friends who kept telling me to read this. My only regret is that I didn’t read it sooner. I will now be spending my thriller reading time in Grant County!<br /></span>

  <span id="freeText14944099533145849237" style="display:none">If you love gritty suspense thrillers, you really must give Karin Slaughter a try. Here's the order in which they should be read: <br /><br /><b>Grant County Series:</b><br /><br />Blindsighted<br />Kisscut<br />A Faint, Cold Fear<br />Indelible<br />Faithless<br />Beyond Reach<br /><br /><b>Will Trent Series</b> <br />These two books can be read (in order) concurrently with the above, but read them before you read the third batch.<br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21717.Triptych__Will_Trent___1_" title="Triptych (Will Trent, #1) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Triptych</a><br />Fractured<br /><br /><b>Georgia Series</b> (merging of two sets of characters)<br /><br />Undone<br />Broken<br />Fallen<br /><br />Fair warning that they are fairly violent and occasionally gruesome...so they are definitely not for the faint of heart.         <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2044968329" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2540743549384897023">I am torn on this one and I am erring on the side of giving the author the benefit of the doubt as it was her first book. It definitely felt like a first effort. (Not that I could do better if I was to try). So, 3 stars for Blindsighted.<br/><br/>The plot was riveting and held my interest. At times, it was very extreme (if fictional violence against women bothers you STAY AWAY), but if you can handle the extreme, the details make it all the more suspenseful.<br/><br/>I felt a bit like some of the plot elements and </span>
  <span id="freeText2540743549384897023" style="display:none">I am torn on this one and I am erring on the side of giving the author the benefit of the doubt as it was her first book. It definitely felt like a first effort. (Not that I could do better if I was to try). So, 3 stars for Blindsighted.<br /><br />The plot was riveting and held my interest. At times, it was very extreme (if fictional violence against women bothers you STAY AWAY), but if you can handle the extreme, the details make it all the more suspenseful.<br /><br />I felt a bit like some of the plot elements and twists were forced. Even though it is supposed to be a mystery until the end, and while I didn't know why it all happened until the end, I felt like the way it was written the "who" was pretty obvious early on.<br /><br />Looks like this was released in 2001 and some of the elements are definitely specific to the time period. Music choices, mention of having something on tape, etc. Just kind of an interesting side note.<br /><br />I am looking forward to trying another as I am sure she hones her craft as she goes on. But, again, this is not too bad of a first effort.</span>

<div id="review_1399242521" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1399242521" />
    <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey"><img alt="Chelsea Humphrey" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585613513p2/47207032.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1399242521?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Chelsea Humphrey" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Chelsea Humphrey" href="/user/show/47207032-chelsea-humphrey">Chelsea Humphrey</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780688174576" href="/book/show/1949796.Blindsighted">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/47207032-chelsea-humphrey?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1399242521" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4103043246834886433">There's something to be said for rereading a book you loved immensely. While I obviously knew "who did it" this go around, it was really a special experience that allowed me to soak up the wonderful characters and marinate in all the feels from these fine southern folks that I haven't spent time with in many moons. Clearly the first go around I was more focused on picking up clues and solving the crime, but this time felt different; it was laid back and easygoing. Gone was the urgent, rushed sen</span>
  <span id="freeText4103043246834886433" style="display:none">There's something to be said for rereading a book you loved immensely. While I obviously knew "who did it" this go around, it was really a special experience that allowed me to soak up the wonderful characters and marinate in all the feels from these fine southern folks that I haven't spent time with in many moons. Clearly the first go around I was more focused on picking up clues and solving the crime, but this time felt different; it was laid back and easygoing. Gone was the urgent, rushed sense of devouring the book (not that there's anything wrong with urgently devouring books), and I was able to experience things from a completely new perspective. Maybe as I grow older I appreciate the fine details, the exquisite style of writing, and the author's talented way of drawing me completely into the story, but I found myself just as gripped by the plot without any of the tension or pressure to fly through and "move on to the next one".<br /><br />Obviously the central case was graphic, both violently and sexually, so it won't be for everyone, but I was so pleased that it remained a concrete 5 stars for me without all the flashy twists blowing my mind from the first go around. If you are looking for top notch characterization in your crime thrillers, you really can't do any better than Karin Slaughter. It's like the woman lives in a different world than we do and sees things I overlook on a daily basis; the tiny details are what really set these stories apart from others in the genre. I know so many people are die hard fans of the Will Trent series, but if you skipped ahead without reading Grant County first I urgently insist that you backtrack and take the time to experience where it all started. There's a tight knit feel in these first 6 books that I have yet to find anywhere else, which is one of many reasons why this series will be one of my all time favorites. Sara + Jeffrey = my favorite couple ever. ❤️❤️❤️<br /><br />**************************<br /><br />A reread for me, but with all these arcs piling up around me I felt I needed to pick up a book that is sentimental and just for me, one with no expectations that I already know I love. I'm really pumped to start this series from the beginning again, as it's one of my all time favorites, and I'm hoping to write a proper review this go around. ❤️</span>
  <a data-text-id="4103043246834886433" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer2887416384159267044">Well after reading BLINDSIGHTED I now consider myself to be a full-blown KARIN SLAUGHTER fan! This is only the second book I have read by her and the first book in her Grant County Series which I thoroughly enjoyed. So this definitely will not be my last and I think that I will probably find myself binge reading the rest of the books in this series.<br/><br/>BLINDSIGHTED by KARIN SLAUGHTER is a gritty, edgy, engrossing, and suspenseful mystery / thriller that had me interested enough to turn those pages a</span>
  <span id="freeText2887416384159267044" style="display:none">Well after reading BLINDSIGHTED I now consider myself to be a full-blown KARIN SLAUGHTER fan! This is only the second book I have read by her and the first book in her Grant County Series which I thoroughly enjoyed. So this definitely will not be my last and I think that I will probably find myself binge reading the rest of the books in this series.<br /><br />BLINDSIGHTED by KARIN SLAUGHTER is a gritty, edgy, engrossing, and suspenseful mystery / thriller that had me interested enough to turn those pages as fast as I could.<br /><br />Trigger warning as this author does go into some graphic detail that might be disturbing for some.<br /><br />The novel kept me interested and guessing with the right amount of clues as the mystery gradually unfolded to the very exciting ending. Although, there was nothing real surprising with the reveal it is the storyline and the way that the author delivers this story is what grabbed my attention and made this book such a good read for me. <br /><br />To sum it all up it was an entertaining, disturbing, exciting, tense, fast-paced, and a quick read with a very satisfying ending. Highly recommend!!<br /><br />Review written and posted on our themed book blog Two Sisters Lost In A Coulee Reading.<br /><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com">https://twosisterslostinacoulee.com</a><br /><br />Coulee: a term applied rather loosely to different landforms, all of which refer to a kind of valley.</span>

<div id="review_2039574480" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2039574480" />
    <a title="Julie " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5210022-julie"><img alt="Julie " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1356906542p2/5210022.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2039574480?book_show_action=true">Jun 27, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Julie " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Julie " href="/user/show/5210022-julie">Julie </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=2017">2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=e-book">e-book</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=overdrive">overdrive</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=thrillers">thrillers</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5210022-julie?shelf=crime">crime</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2039574480" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15910845926025805672">Blindsighted by Karin Slaughter is a 2015 Harper publication. <br/><br/>This is the first book in the Grant County series, which was originally published way back in 2002. I have read this book before, a long time ago, before Goodreads had even launched. <br/><br/>However, I decided to start the Grant County series over, despite having read a few of them already. It’s a long story, but basically, I got some of the Grant County books mixed up with the Will Trent series, which caused a great deal of confusion, for me</span>
  <span id="freeText15910845926025805672" style="display:none">Blindsighted by Karin Slaughter is a 2015 Harper publication. <br /><br />This is the first book in the Grant County series, which was originally published way back in 2002. I have read this book before, a long time ago, before Goodreads had even launched. <br /><br />However, I decided to start the Grant County series over, despite having read a few of them already. It’s a long story, but basically, I got some of the Grant County books mixed up with the Will Trent series, which caused a great deal of confusion, for me, which is something I did a lot until GR came along to help me organize my books and before I recieved valuable hints and suggestions from other readers. <br /><br />So, although I know how things work out for some of the characters in future installments, I want to understand the full story, and refresh my memory about a few things before I continue with the Trent series. <br /><br /><br />Sara is a pediatrician and works part time as a coroner. The part time work puts her directly in contact with her ex-husband, Jeffrey, a man she has a complicated history with and with whom she still carries a torch. <br /><br />But, when Jeffrey’s deputy, Lena, loses her sister in a very violent way, it stirs up bad memories for Sara and forces her to work up close and personal with her Jeffrey while they try to put a killer behind bars. <br /><br />This is a very gritty crime thriller with some pretty gruesome and lurid descriptions, which is certainly not for the faint of heart. <br /><br />There’s also some fantastic personal interactions, some of which nearly choked me up. Wow. I had forgotten how good this book was! <br /><br /> It has perfect pacing, well-timed twists, and in -depth characterizations that are very rare for a ‘first in a series’ novel, and of course, let’s not forget that stunning shocker at the end!! Although this book was written fifteen years ago, it stands up well to the test of time and blew me away, even knowing all I know now. <br /><br />So, if you have started the Will Trent series without reading this series first, I still recommend picking these up. If you haven’t read Will Trent yet, I STRONGLY urge you to read the Grant County books first because it will really help you understand the backstories that crossover into the Trent series later. <br /><br /><br />4.5 stars<br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

          </span>

      </span>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1034000185" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12750591373558024528">This was not my first book by Slaughter. I read this book after reading Cop town and Pretty Girls and now I am hooked. Slaughter has quickly become one of my favorite mystery writers. She is a gritty and intelligent writer. I love the research she puts into her books. Having a background in Forensics, I really appreciate her books and the research she puts into this.<br/><br/>In Blindsighted, a professor is found murdered in a restaurant. Her Murder hits very close to home to Sara, who is the town's Pedia</span>
  <span id="freeText12750591373558024528" style="display:none">This was not my first book by Slaughter. I read this book after reading Cop town and Pretty Girls and now I am hooked. Slaughter has quickly become one of my favorite mystery writers. She is a gritty and intelligent writer. I love the research she puts into her books. Having a background in Forensics, I really appreciate her books and the research she puts into this.<br /><br />In Blindsighted, a professor is found murdered in a restaurant. Her Murder hits very close to home to Sara, who is the town's Pediatrician and Coroner. It is also Sara who discovers the body. The professor turns out to the twin sister of a police officer who works for Sara's ex-husband, Jeffrey.<br /><br />Will Sara's past hold the key to solving this case? What will happen between her and her ex-husband Jeffrey?<br /><br />As stated above, I love Slaughter's attention to detail. I love the police work involved, the investigations, the forensics, even the autopsies are well done in this book. But mostly, I love the relationships between the characters. I love the love story between Sara and Jeffrey. Just enough is told to make me like them both. To get me involved in their history and continued story. <br /><br />Plus, well there is a killer on the loose. Who is it. Will there be more victims? Will the police save the day?<br /><br />I'll never tell. Pick up this book and read it already!<br /><br />see more of my reviews at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.openbookpost.com">www.openbookpost.com</a></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer541507916" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13849748458374782840"><b>Blindsighted: Karin Slaughter's first Sara Linton novel</b><br/><br/>And the publishers announce:<br/><br/><b>First there was Patricia Cornwell!</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1151.beta.photobucket.com/user/mmcsullivan/media/PatriciaCornwell_zps78f8f3a9.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380410480i/804894.jpg' alt=' photo PatriciaCornwell_zps78f8f3a9.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>THEN there was Kathy Reichs!</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1151.beta.photobucket.com/user/mmcsullivan/media/bones_reichs_388_zpsd5ca45bd.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380410481i/804895.jpg' alt=' photo bones_reichs_388_zpsd5ca45bd.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><b>NOW GET READY FOR KARIN SLAUGHTER!</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1151.beta.photobucket.com/user/mmcsullivan/media/KarinSlaughter_zps1fcf68e9.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380410481i/804896.jpg' alt=' photo KarinSlaughter_zps1fcf68e9.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><i>Karin Slaughter</i><br/><br/>Welcome to Grant County, Georgia. Don't look for it on a Georgia map. It isn't there. And in this fictional County, there's a fictional town. It's a small town called Heartsdale, somewhere around Madison, but before you hit Augusta.<br/><br/>Eddie Linton and Daughters is a plumbing company in town. But </span>
  <span id="freeText13849748458374782840" style="display:none"><b>Blindsighted: Karin Slaughter's first Sara Linton novel</b><br><br>And the publishers announce:<br><br><b>First there was Patricia Cornwell!</b><br><br><a href="http://s1151.beta.photobucket.com/user/mmcsullivan/media/PatriciaCornwell_zps78f8f3a9.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380410480i/804894.jpg" alt=" photo PatriciaCornwell_zps78f8f3a9.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>THEN there was Kathy Reichs!</b><br><br><a href="http://s1151.beta.photobucket.com/user/mmcsullivan/media/bones_reichs_388_zpsd5ca45bd.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380410481i/804895.jpg" alt=" photo bones_reichs_388_zpsd5ca45bd.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><b>NOW GET READY FOR KARIN SLAUGHTER!</b><br><br><a href="http://s1151.beta.photobucket.com/user/mmcsullivan/media/KarinSlaughter_zps1fcf68e9.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380410481i/804896.jpg" alt=" photo KarinSlaughter_zps1fcf68e9.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>Karin Slaughter</i><br><br>Welcome to Grant County, Georgia. Don't look for it on a Georgia map. It isn't there. And in this fictional County, there's a fictional town. It's a small town called Heartsdale, somewhere around Madison, but before you hit Augusta.<br><br>Eddie Linton and Daughters is a plumbing company in town. But it should be Linton and Daughter. Tessa works with her father. Sara grew up and went to medical school and became a pediatrician. <br><br>After medical school Sara returns home and takes over the town medical clinic. The nearest hospital is in Augusta. She married Jeff Tolliver, the County Sheriff, but divorced him after he cheated on her with the town sign painter. <br><br>Life's complicated when your Ex is the Sheriff and you're not only the town's pediatrician, but also the County Coroner. You bump into your Ex a lot more than you might like. Actually, Jeff wouldn't mind patching things up. After all, he only had that affair because he wanted Sara to need him as much as he needed her. Uh-huh. What? Could this be a new genre? "Crimance?"<br><br>Sara definitely doesn't want Jeff back in her life. She's dated the town pharmacist, Jeb, off and on. It hasn't been anything serious. Sara really doesn't have the time.<br><br>Things turn nasty when Sara has lunch with her sister Tessa down at Pete's Diner. She steps into the bathroom to wash her hands and finds herself in the middle of a crime scene. Sybil Adams is sitting on the john. Someone has carved a cross into her. Sybil dies in convulsions in Sara's arms as she bleeds out on the bathroom floor.<br><br>From whence does the title come? Why, from <i>Belladonna</i> from the Italian meaning "beautiful woman." Traditionally the plant was used to cause dilation of the pupils to make a woman appear more seductive. Use too much of the stuff, you become so sensitive to light you can see nothing, and it's a powerful hallucinogenic, causing paralysis, loss of memory, and convulsions.<br><br><a href="http://s1151.beta.photobucket.com/user/mmcsullivan/media/Atropa_belladonna_zps0dcc9669.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380410481i/804897.jpg" alt=" photo Atropa_belladonna_zps0dcc9669.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>Belladona</i><br><br>Sybil was blind. Hmmm...in Roman mythology Sybil was a "Seeress." Well, maybe it was just a coincidental choice and not an attempt at irony. She was a professor at the small college. She was also a lesbian. Was it a hate crime? More conflict rises because her sister Lena is one of Sheriff Tolliver's Detectives. She's out to find her own justice for her sister's death.<br><br>Sara's autopsy reveals that Sybil was also raped and sodomized. A second victim is found draped across Sarah's car. She had been crucified in x form, and repeatedly raped and sodomized. She was also stabbed. Sara prevents her death by cracking her chest and massaging her heart. When this young woman begins to tell of her experience, Jeff realizes he's got an escalating serial rapist/killer on his hands.<br><br>Slaughter relentlessly turns up the pace when Jeff's detective Lena, Sibyl's sister is the next woman to disappear. Slaughter has the ability to keep you flipping the pages to see what happens next.<br><br>Could Sara be the next victim, Jeff worries. Can he find his missing detective?<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21718.Blindsighted__Grant_County___1_" title="Blindsighted (Grant County, #1) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Blindsighted</a> is a decent series debut. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12504.Karin_Slaughter" title="Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Karin Slaughter</a> has sold a gazillion books. The book blurbs glow.<br><br>BUT: I wish I could have liked this book more. The herrings herein are very, very, red. There's the homophobic doper. And a ridiculous stab at an incident of token racism, when some townsmen assume that an aged black man musta dun it. OH, PLEASE! C'MON!<br><br>I anticipated the identity of the perp long before the end. While on the surface of things, Sara appears proficient in her forensic skills, she is a pediatrician, not a pathologist. If Sara ever makes it to court, it wouldn't be pretty. Oh. Dang. Spoiler alert: If the perp never survives, you don't have to worry about witness qualification. <br><br>And, by the way, the Georgia Bureau of Investigation has a death investigation division with either four to five regional laboratories staffed with pathologists. Georgia uses a Medical Examiner System. The Coroner calls for an autopsy, but bodies are transported to the labs for the autopsies. Now, I do understand that six Georgia counties are not covered by GBI, so considering Grant County is fictional anyway, well, heck this is a work of fiction. Interestingly, Slaughter also refers to Sara as a medical examiner in one paragraph in which she also calls her a coroner.<br><br>I'm jaded. Twenty-eight years in a District Attorney's Office will do that to you. If you think I'm too hard in my assessment of Karin Slaughter, don't get me started on John Grisham. D.A. does NOT stand for dumb ass, Mr. Grisham. <br><br>One thing I must acknowledge. Karin Slaughter has the dynamics of rape and men who rape down with great accuracy. For the dialogue, pacing, and that knowledge, I give this 3.5 our of five stars.<br><br>Having said all that, of course I already have the second book in the series. I admit I like it when the good guys win.<br><br> </span>
  <a data-text-id="13849748458374782840" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer966177788" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3272503040601816730">"Blindsighted" by Karin Slaughter, is the first book in the Grant County Series. If you love reading gritty suspense thrillers, you really must give Karin Slaughter a try. Karin Slaughter books are not for the faint of heart. Being a avid reader of mystery/suspense thrillers, this is the most graphic book I have read in this category. <br/>The Forensics, the police work, etc are all exceptionally well done, and her characters are involving.<br/><br/>A small Georgia town erupts in panic when a young college pro</span>
  <span id="freeText3272503040601816730" style="display:none">"Blindsighted" by Karin Slaughter, is the first book in the Grant County Series. If you love reading gritty suspense thrillers, you really must give Karin Slaughter a try. Karin Slaughter books are not for the faint of heart. Being a avid reader of mystery/suspense thrillers, this is the most graphic book I have read in this category. <br />The Forensics, the police work, etc are all exceptionally well done, and her characters are involving.<br /><br />A small Georgia town erupts in panic when a young college professor is found brutally mutilated in the local diner. But it's only when town pediatrician and coroner Sara Linton does the autopsy that the full extent of the killer's twisted work becomes clear.<br /><br />Sara's ex-husband, police chief Jeffrey Tolliver, leads the investigation - and then the suspense builds when another local woman is found crucified a few days later. But he's got more than a sadistic serial killer on his hands. The county's sole female detective, Lena Adams - the first victim's sister, wants her own justice.<br /><br />But it is Sara who holds the key to finding the killer. A secret from her past could reveal the psychopath.<br /><br /><br />The suspense part of the book was very well written and had the pages flying by. There is an unresolved love angle in here for the Doc and her ex-husband, who just happens to be the chief of police. Looking forward to continuing to read the next book in the series,"Kisscut".<br /><br /><br /><br /> <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /> <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /> <br /><br /><br /> <br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /><br /></span>

<div id="review_1379789652" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1379789652" />
    <a title="Mo" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11856352-mo"><img alt="Mo" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1371247812p2/11856352.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1379789652?book_show_action=true">Sep 01, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mo" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mo" href="/user/show/11856352-mo">Mo</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/6646562-blindsighted">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1379789652" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4726972285968020641">This is Ms Slaughter's debut novel so maybe I should cut her some slack. I don't know what it was about it that just did not grab me. <div id="review_956760145" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/956760145" />
    <a title="Tim The Enchanter" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5654692-tim-the-enchanter"><img alt="Tim The Enchanter" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1386188040p2/5654692.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tim The Enchanter" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tim The Enchanter" href="/user/show/5654692-tim-the-enchanter">Tim The Enchanter</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=my-ebooks">my-ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=mystery">mystery</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=3-5-stars">3-5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=crime">crime</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5654692-tim-the-enchanter?shelf=police-procedural">police-procedural</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer956760145" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9126020845136730138">Posted to <a href='http://theliterarylawyer.ca/blindsighted-karin-slaughter-grant-county-1/' rel='nofollow noopener'> The Literary Lawyer.ca </a><br/><br/><br/><b> <u> Beautiful Body that is Missing a Soul - 3.5 Stars </u> </b><br/><br/>This was my first foray into the world of Karin Slaughter. Her world is filled with interesting characters, personal drama and a fair share of deranged individuals. I did enjoy the book. The writing was very good, the characters were interesting and the plot was good. That said, it seemed to be missing something. Something I am having a hard time putting my finger on. For all the positives, the story still lac</span>
  <span id="freeText9126020845136730138" style="display:none">Posted to <a href="http://theliterarylawyer.ca/blindsighted-karin-slaughter-grant-county-1/" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Literary Lawyer.ca </a><br /><br /><br /><b> <u> Beautiful Body that is Missing a Soul - 3.5 Stars </u> </b><br /><br />This was my first foray into the world of Karin Slaughter. Her world is filled with interesting characters, personal drama and a fair share of deranged individuals. I did enjoy the book. The writing was very good, the characters were interesting and the plot was good. That said, it seemed to be missing something. Something I am having a hard time putting my finger on. For all the positives, the story still lacks.<br /><br /> Plot summary <br /><br />The story shifts through three major points of view. Sara, the town's coroner and a pediatrician. Jeffery, the ex-husband of Sara and the town's chief of police and Lena, a deputy on the force and sister of the first victim. The story opens with the murder of Lena's sister. Sara finds her body in restaurant washroom where she has been killed and brutalized. Unfortunately, this is not last body as others go missing and crimes contain similar ritualistic elements. As the story progresses as the crimes become personal for all parties involved and secrets from the past may hold the key to unlocking the mysteries of the murders.<br /><br /> The Good <br /><br /><b> Well Crafted </b><br /><br />This was one well crafted novel. This was nominated the Barry Award for Best First Novel and it was certainly good enough to have won it. Karin Slaughter wrote a book that was taunt, thrilling and as polished as those with much more experience. There was an interesting storyline with red herrings, misdirection and slight of hand. While the beginning of the novel lagged, the pace picked up significantly in the middle of the book<br /><br />There was significant drama amongst the characters. While I despise excessive romance in my novels and roll my eyes when the story becomes overly emotional, the author deftly walked the line on this point. There are complex relationships each with their own histories and developments.<br /><br /> The Bad <br /><br /><b> But Its Missing Something... </b><br /><br />Despite all of the positive elements, the novel did not feel complete. Despite a good storyline, good character development and thrills and chills, the story may have been a victim of its own slick execution. While I enjoyed the story and was interested in the outcome, I did not connect with the characters. By the end, I was interested to see if my theories were correct but I did not care about the characters. While the body of the novel was solid and looked good, the lacked some soul<br /><br /><b> Final Thoughts </b><br /><br />A slow first half and a lack of soul and emotion hurt my rating on this one. That said, it is an excellent and well crafted first novel. Karin Slaughter has had a long and successful career and I am confident that her skill improved as she gained experience. Overall, a worthwhile read but not one that I will list amongst my favorites.<br /><br /><b>  Content Advisories  </b><br /><br />It is difficult to find commentary on the sex/violence/language content of book if you are interested. I make an effort to give you the information so you can make an informed decision before reading. *Disclaimer* I do not take note or count the occurrences of adult language as I read. I am simply giving approximations.<br /><br />Scale 1 - Lowest 5 - Highest<br /><br /> Sex  - <b> 3.5 </b><br /><br />Much of the sexual content is related to a series of sex crimes. There is one moderately graphic scene of a sexual assault. There are several more far more disturbing elements are revealed in the investigation of sexual assaults. There is some disturbing sodomy involved and other elements that are violent.<br /><br /> Language  - <b> 3 </b><br /><br />There is moderate use of mild obscenities and low usage of the f-word. There is also some low use of sexual derived adult language.<br /><br /> Violence  - <b> 4 </b><br /><br />There are some disturbing elements of violence in the novel (see sexual content). There are some moderately high graphic description of the violence. There are some ritualistic elements in the violence amongst multiple murders. Readers who are moderately sensitive to sexual violence should avoid this book.</span>
  <a data-text-id="9126020845136730138" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_150348939" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/150348939" />
    <a title="Ray Daniel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4877068-ray-daniel"><img alt="Ray Daniel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1461446724p2/4877068.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/150348939?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ray Daniel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ray Daniel" href="/user/show/4877068-ray-daniel">Ray Daniel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer150348939" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5465279045602026777">I hardly every rank a book with five stars. To get there the book needs to do three things:<br/><br/>1. Turn off my internal editor--As a writer I have an internal editor who screens everything I read and tries to improve it. It takes a great book to get him to shut up and let me enjoy the story. Blindsighted shut him down in two chapters.<br/><br/>2. Invade my life--I read every day on the elliptical trainer. But Blindsighted had me reading through all my airline flights, in the limo, and on my couch. I would wake</span>
  <span id="freeText5465279045602026777" style="display:none">I hardly every rank a book with five stars. To get there the book needs to do three things:<br /><br />1. Turn off my internal editor--As a writer I have an internal editor who screens everything I read and tries to improve it. It takes a great book to get him to shut up and let me enjoy the story. Blindsighted shut him down in two chapters.<br /><br />2. Invade my life--I read every day on the elliptical trainer. But Blindsighted had me reading through all my airline flights, in the limo, and on my couch. I would wake up in the morning and wonder what was going to happen to these characters.<br /><br />3. Make me sad when it's over--Someone once said that finishing a great book is like saying goodbye to a friend. Finishing Blindsighted was a bittersweet experience. I'll miss it.<br /><br />The book has powerful characters, great writing, and a chilling plot. What more could you want?</span>
  <a data-text-id="5465279045602026777" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer17572816496107780415">This book was voted as our June Book Read by our group " A Good Thriller"<br/><br/>Happy this book was voted as have enjoyed quite a few of Karin Slaughter books, although good to read this book as her debut book and the introduction of her character Sara Linton.<br/><br/>Karin Slaughter--a wonderful name for a crime/mystery writer--sets her novel in a small town in Georgia. Nothing much happens in Heartsdale, and the local pediatrician, Sara Linton, also works as the coroner. Sara meets her younger sister for lunc</span>
  <span id="freeText17572816496107780415" style="display:none">This book was voted as our June Book Read by our group " A Good Thriller"<br /><br />Happy this book was voted as have enjoyed quite a few of Karin Slaughter books, although good to read this book as her debut book and the introduction of her character Sara Linton.<br /><br />Karin Slaughter--a wonderful name for a crime/mystery writer--sets her novel in a small town in Georgia. Nothing much happens in Heartsdale, and the local pediatrician, Sara Linton, also works as the coroner. Sara meets her younger sister for lunch at the local diner one afternoon and stumbles upon a grisly scene. The twin sister of a local detective has been viciously attacked, mutilated, and raped. It's not long before another victim surfaces, and Sara works along with her ex-husband who also happens to be the Chief of Police to try to track down this sick killer. All the while, Sara has her own tortured past as well as her strained relationship with her ex-husband to deal with. In this small town where everyone knows everyone else, who could possibly be the twisted rapist murderer?<br /><br />Slaughter seems to have done her research for this novel. The medical information alone is quite interesting, and the dialogue and characters are believable, a tough subject dealing with serial killers in this day and age. It's well written, keeps you guessing and keeps to a fast pace with a chilling build up to the end in this powerful story.<br /><br />Now reading my BOOK PAL book for June , The Bone House by Brian Freeman, my first book by this author, who is joining us for a Q &amp; A in August.</span>

          </span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2435770275" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16592541860964325436">I’m always in the mood for some Slaughterhouse!<br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1530130370ra/25868996.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12504.Karin_Slaughter' title='Karin Slaughter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Karin Slaughter</a> can write some dark thrillers, and I can't help but love every disturbingly graphic word. Her talent is in her characters, the story's flow and pace, and the magical ability to keep her readers grasping for the next word. In terms of mystery, I knew who the perp was at around the 50% mark. Did that stop my enjoyment? Not even a little bit. Slaughter writes books that you can't put down, because the storyline is so involved. It's not </span>
  <span id="freeText16592541860964325436" style="display:none">I’m always in the mood for some Slaughterhouse!<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1530130370ra/25868996.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12504.Karin_Slaughter" title="Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Karin Slaughter</a> can write some dark thrillers, and I can't help but love every disturbingly graphic word. Her talent is in her characters, the story's flow and pace, and the magical ability to keep her readers grasping for the next word. In terms of mystery, I knew who the perp was at around the 50% mark. Did that stop my enjoyment? Not even a little bit. Slaughter writes books that you can't put down, because the storyline is so involved. It's not just a crime to be solved (although the forensic element is fantastically gruesome in my opinion). It's family, town, and workplace dynamics. It's a history of events. It's the skillful development of characters that you can effortlessly connect with, and every action they take makes complete sense to you. <br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21718.Blindsighted__Grant_County___1_" title="Blindsighted (Grant County, #1) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Blindsighted</a> was Slaughter's debut novel (and what a debut!!), and I still kick myself for not finding her sooner. I started my "slaughterhouse" bookshelf with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25574782.Pretty_Girls" title="Pretty Girls by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Pretty Girls</a> and have been hooked ever since. I am making a slow but heartfelt effort to play catch up, and with every title, I'm astounded by this woman's work. Better late than never!<br><br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21718.Blindsighted__Grant_County___1_" title="Blindsighted (Grant County, #1) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Blindsighted</a> is the first installment in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/12504.Karin_Slaughter" title="Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Karin Slaughter</a>'s <u>Grant County</u> series. The series consists of the following installments as of June 2018:<br>#1-<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21718.Blindsighted__Grant_County___1_" title="Blindsighted (Grant County, #1) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Blindsighted</a><br>#2-<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21719.Kisscut__Grant_County___2_" title="Kisscut (Grant County, #2) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Kisscut</a><br>#3-<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21721.A_Faint_Cold_Fear__Grant_County___3_" title="A Faint Cold Fear (Grant County, #3) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">A Faint Cold Fear</a><br>#4-<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/182012.Indelible__Grant_County___4_" title="Indelible (Grant County, #4) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Indelible</a><br>#5-<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21722.Faithless__Grant_County___5_" title="Faithless (Grant County, #5) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Faithless</a><br>#6-<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21720.Beyond_Reach__Grant_County___6_" title="Beyond Reach (Grant County, #6) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Beyond Reach</a><br><br><b>My favorite quote:</b><br>Surprisingly none, but it still got a blazing 5-stars from me!</span>
  <a data-text-id="16592541860964325436" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

    <a title="Stephanie Nicholas" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/92879415-stephanie-nicholas"><img alt="Stephanie Nicholas" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1548828666p2/92879415.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2930882187?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie Nicholas" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie Nicholas" href="/user/show/92879415-stephanie-nicholas">Stephanie Nicholas</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2930882187" class="readable"
              >

<div id="review_1368496169" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1368496169" />
    <a title="Brandi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4765786-brandi"><img alt="Brandi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1431565587p2/4765786.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1368496169?book_show_action=true">Aug 19, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brandi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brandi" href="/user/show/4765786-brandi">Brandi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4765786-brandi?shelf=cant-bear-to-finish">cant-bear-to-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1368496169" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15890919549997859634"><a href='http://thebookgeek.co.uk/' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <br/>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>Well, this didn't work for me at all - I haven't even wanted to pick it up for two days. Our main character was more scared than I could believe considering <u>she's the coroner and dead bodies aren't foreign to her</u>. I believed the shock she felt when she first saw the body, because you're not expecting something like that ever, but after that all her nerves were just annoying to me. Or how she was cradling the victim when the cop came, as if she were really close to this person, but she was</span>
  <span id="freeText15890919549997859634" style="display:none"><a href="http://thebookgeek.co.uk/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1379777457i/368079.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Well, this didn't work for me at all - I haven't even wanted to pick it up for two days. Our main character was more scared than I could believe considering <u>she's the coroner and dead bodies aren't foreign to her</u>. I believed the shock she felt when she first saw the body, because you're not expecting something like that ever, but after that all her nerves were just annoying to me. Or how she was cradling the victim when the cop came, as if she were really close to this person, but she wasn't, so why the forehead stroking and all that? <br><br>The guy has been a cop for TWENTY years, and the first half had been spent in a place where murders weren't uncommon (he says not a week went by without investigating one), yet when he learns of this new murder he freaks out. He says how it literally takes his breath away when he sees the scene, and at one point gets lightheaded when the CORONER has to point out the murder is probably not a simple murder, but in the next fricken sentence he's thinking how he's seen that kind of thing before. And this gem: "<i>"What?" He asked, his voice echoing slightly on the cellular.</i>" What the fuck is that?! Where's the finesse and superb writing that made Pretty Girls so unputdownable?! UGH. <br><br>Another cop, but at least this one had an actual personal connection to the murder victim, is searching for anything that could help shed light on who did it, and she's looking for the diary, but it's in braille since the victim was blind, and as the victim's lover picks it up to translate it the cop thinks: "For some reason, Lena got the impression she was touching the pages because [the victim] had, as if she could absorb some sense of [the victim] rather than just words." <b>For. Some. Reason.</b> Ok. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1440435208ra/15974880.gif" width="300" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>This book does not read like Slaughter's <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/25574782.Pretty_Girls" title="Pretty Girls by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Pretty Girls</a> at all. I had zero complaints for Pretty Girls, but I can't even bring myself to finish this one. The only thing I like about it is that it's about adults and not teens and a ritualistic-ish murder plot would have been great to read about. <br><br>In the end, the reviews are great so people clearly aren't bothered by the same shit I was, but I can't bring myself to recommend this one.<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="15890919549997859634" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_177450532" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177450532" />
    <a title="Jonetta" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4876540-jonetta"><img alt="Jonetta" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1329083158p2/4876540.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/177450532?book_show_action=true">Jun 17, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jonetta" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jonetta" href="/user/show/4876540-jonetta">Jonetta</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="ebook 9780061796814" href="/book/show/10181838-blindsighted">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4876540-jonetta?shelf=group-read">group-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4876540-jonetta?shelf=mystery-suspense">mystery-suspense</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177450532" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10021027214444763775">Sarah Linton is a pediatrician and the coroner for the town of Heartsdale in Grant County, Georgia. If that wasn't a weird enough combination, her ex-husband, Jeffrey Tolliver, is the town's police chief. I knew from the start this was going to be a different kind of story. <br/><br/><b>The crime</b><br/>Sarah goes to the local diner for lunch with her sister. She's a little late and the lunch crowd is pretty much gone. When she goes to the restroom, she finds Sibyl Adams, a professor at the local college who is also</span>
  <span id="freeText10021027214444763775" style="display:none">Sarah Linton is a pediatrician and the coroner for the town of Heartsdale in Grant County, Georgia. If that wasn't a weird enough combination, her ex-husband, Jeffrey Tolliver, is the town's police chief. I knew from the start this was going to be a different kind of story. <br /><br /><b>The crime</b><br />Sarah goes to the local diner for lunch with her sister. She's a little late and the lunch crowd is pretty much gone. When she goes to the restroom, she finds Sibyl Adams, a professor at the local college who is also blind, covered in blood in one of the stalls. She's been brutally stabbed and assaulted and Sarah tries but can't save her. During the autopsy, she discovers just how demented her killer really is. <br /><br /><b>The issues</b><br />There's quite a bit of inbreeding in this town. Sibyl was Detective Lena Adam's sister and she's difficult to deal with under good circumstances. She insists on being part of the investigation and Jeffrey doesn't have a deep investigative bench to keep her on the sidelines. When another woman is assaulted in a similar manner, it's clear that they've got a possible serial killer to deal with. <br /><br /><b>The mystery and suspense</b><br />There are a lot of angles, including an overlay of bigotry and insubordination amongst the police ranks. Jeffrey is also trying to get back into Sarah's life while trying to work with her to solve the cases. She's withholding some major stuff that could possibly impact the case but doesn't want to revisit her troubled past. When a third person goes missing, it strikes even closer to home. <br /><br /><b>The bottom line</b><br />This is the first book in the series and it is chilling. All those involved in the case, while talented, have some major issues in their personal lives that resurface throughout the course of the investigation. That just made the story even more exciting and frustrating. It wasn't all that easy to figure out whodunit but it wasn't impossible either. If this first book is a measure of those to come, I'm in for an incredible journey. The book is not without its flaws but they're not significant enough to detract from your overall enjoyment. Oh, and it's not for the squeamish. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10021027214444763775" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3357984278" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15811343650235779985">I had this persistent, nagging sense of déjà vu the WHOLE time I was reading this book—and just before the murderer was revealed it hit me like a sledgehammer that I have indeed read <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21718.Blindsighted__Grant_County___1_' title='Blindsighted (Grant County, #1) by Karin Slaughter' rel='nofollow noopener'>Blindsighted</a> before 😂 I'm usually so diligent about recording books I've read on my Goodreads but this one somehow slipped through the cracks, urgh!<br/><br/>◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️<br/><br/>I'm not really one to reread mystery/thrillers, but if there ever were ones I'd reread, they'd without a doubt be Karin Slaug</span>
  <span id="freeText15811343650235779985" style="display:none">I had this persistent, nagging sense of déjà vu the WHOLE time I was reading this book—and just before the murderer was revealed it hit me like a sledgehammer that I have indeed read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/21718.Blindsighted__Grant_County___1_" title="Blindsighted (Grant County, #1) by Karin Slaughter" rel="nofollow noopener">Blindsighted</a> before 😂 I'm usually so diligent about recording books I've read on my Goodreads but this one somehow slipped through the cracks, urgh!<br /><br />◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️◻️<br /><br />I'm not really one to reread mystery/thrillers, but if there ever were ones I'd reread, they'd without a doubt be Karin Slaughter's. Fleshed-out characters, consistent pacing, and compulsively readable storylines featuring bad, bad men—<br /><br />Like, how does she come UP with this stuff? It's so morbid and dark and gruesome, and her murderers' twisted psyches are in a league of their own. I'd be simultaneously thrilled and terrified to have a chance to poke around in her head.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>Bottom line:</u>
</b> You don't think anyone will go there? She will go there. You never thought that anatomically possible? Oh, it's <i>possible.</i> KARIN SLAUGHTER LEAVES NO STONE UNTURNED, Y'ALL.</span>

//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('GUlnLoEUGWnURGE+s8X6pRaDLF2E/QcuF089swuD/d/LctQ8MCQVerQBikDzDHhO9XEycVswW3/bFy3tPFFo+A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('nAlYt65iXG84kWMmjREOlh+930A1qohTpNeApp0tGe9OMuulH1JQfFjUiFjN2Ix9/E/BbOpn1AJoj5D4qv+MyA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer9296071252973859613">Karin Slaughter is one of the world’s most popular and acclaimed storytellers. Published in 120 countries with more than 35 million copies sold across the globe, her nineteen novels include the Grant County and Will Trent books, as well as the Edgar-nominated COP TOWN and the instant NEW YORK TIMES bestselling novels PRETTY GIRLS, THE GOOD DAUGHTER, and PIECES OF HER. Her most recent book, THE LAS</span>
  <span id="freeText9296071252973859613" style="display:none">Karin Slaughter is one of the world’s most popular and acclaimed storytellers. Published in 120 countries with more than 35 million copies sold across the globe, her nineteen novels include the Grant County and Will Trent books, as well as the Edgar-nominated COP TOWN and the instant NEW YORK TIMES bestselling novels PRETTY GIRLS, THE GOOD DAUGHTER, and PIECES OF HER. Her most recent book, THE LAST WIDOW, features Sara Linton and Will Trent. Slaughter is the founder of the Save the Libraries project—a nonprofit organization established to support libraries and library programming. A native of Georgia, Karin Slaughter lives in Atlanta. Her standalone novels PIECES OF HER, THE GOOD DAUGHTER, and COP TOWN are in development for film and television.<br /><br /><br /><b>Facebook:</b> <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://Facebook.com/AuthorKarinSlaughter">Facebook.com/AuthorKarinSlaughter</a> <br /><br /><b>Website</b>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.karinslaughter.com/">http://www.karinslaughter.com/</a><br /><br /><b>Instagram</b>: <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="https://www.instagram.com/karinslaughterauthor/">https://www.instagram.com/karinslaugh...</a><br /></span>
